{"date":"20260122","title":"Riemann Liquid Spatio-Temporal Graph","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q1ugd9NYPUA","description":"The End of \"Flat Earth\" AI\nBoth new research pre-prints deliver a unified wake-up call: Current Deep Learning architectures are too \"flat\" to model reality. It demonstrates that to understand causality in complex systems (like traffic, biology, or robotics), we must abandon the \"turn-based game\" of discrete steps and embrace Continuous Dynamics on Curved Manifolds. \n\nBy forcing the AI to solve differential equations on Riemannian surfaces rather than flat planes, we mathematically constrain the model. It stops hallucinating impossible trajectories and starts respecting the topological \"shape\" of the data, finally allowing AI to understand how change happens, not just that it happened.\n\nCorrecting the Privacy of Mind (Chimpanzee Study)\nThe Chimpanzee paper reveals the cognitive gap. It proves that our \"Superintelligences\" currently lack the epistemic isolation skills of a primate. {"date":"20260105","title":"Princeton: NEW Self Correcting AI Transformer (Deep Delta)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bZbdKo_EAoY","description":"Based on two new AI research pre-prints by Princeton University (see below)  I design a new transformer architecture, by combining the hardware and software insights from these pre-prints and I call this new AI Transformer: \"Self-Correcting Delta Transformer\". A new transformer that can forget incorrect reasoning traces. \n\nThe Pathology of Additive Reasoning:\nRecent empirical rigor dismantles the myth of intrinsic self-correction in current Large Language Models. Analysis of over 1 million reasoning traces reveals that spontaneous \"Aha!\" moments, where a model pauses to rethink, are currently statistically correlated with inference collapse rather than insight.\n\nThis behavioral pathology is rooted in the thermodynamic rigidity of the standard additive residual connection (x+F(x)): once an erroneous feature is written to the hidden state, the architecture lacks the physical mechanism to remove it. Consequently, high-entropy \"corrections\" are merely stacked atop the initial error, leading to \"Residual Accumulation\": a noisy state where the ghost of a flawed hypothesis actively interferes with the new reasoning path, rendering the \"insight\" an illusion.\nBy combining two new AI research ArXiv pre-prints from Princeton University (see below)  we can build a new Transformer architecture, which I call \" Self-Correcting DELTA Transformer\". \n\nThe Geometric Cure:\nDeep Delta Learning introduces the architectural primitive required to turn this illusion into reality: the generalised Householder Operator. By replacing the standard accumulation layer with a learnable geometric transformation A(X), the network gains the ability to perform Destructive Interference (!) on its own residual stream. \n\nThis operator acts as a differentiable \"Eraser,\" allowing the model to mathematically annihilate specific feature subspaces (via orthogonal projection when β→1) before injecting new information. This creates a unified Write-Erase mechanism, enabling the network to physically flush \"bad thoughts\" from its working memory and execute a clean, high-fidelity state update.\n\nAll rights w/ authors: \n\"Deep Delta Learning\"\nYifan Zhang1 Yifeng Liu2 Mengdi Wang1 Quanquan Gu2\nfrom\n1 Princeton University \n2 University of California, Los Angeles\n\n\"The Illusion of Insight in Reasoning Models\"\nLiv G. d’Aliberti\nPrinceton University\nDepartment of Computer Science\nPrinceton, NJ, USA\nManoel Horta Ribeiro\nPrinceton University\nDepartment of Computer Science\nPrinceton, NJ, USA\n\n#airesearch \n#princetonuniversity \n#aiexplained \n#computer \n#maths \n#scienceexplained \n#science \n#aitransformation"}

{"date":"20251216","title":"Breaking Logic Limits: NEW AI Solution Paths (GPT-5.2 high+)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=r5tAzwQuNAo","description":"Breaking Logic Limits: NEW AI Solution Paths for your LOCAL LLM.\nHow to optimize your local LLM with a simple trick.\n\nInstruction set you can paste:\n\nVariant 1: Guaranteed-shortest via explicit state-space search\n1) **Restate the problem as a shortest-path task.**  \n   Identify: initial conditions, goal conditions, allowed actions, action costs (usually “1 step per action”), constraints (resource minimums, forbidden moves, limited use of stochastic actions, etc.).\n\n2) **Define a complete state representation before reasoning.**  \n   A “state” must contain *everything that can change future outcomes*, including:  \n   - Position/progress variables (where you are in the process)  \n   - Resources (energy, tokens, time budget, etc.)  \n   - Global modes/flags/toggles  \n   - Inventory/permissions/codes  \n   - Any counters (e.g., “every 5th use gives bonus”)  \n   - Required short histories (e.g., last k actions, last k states) if rules depend on them  \n   - Whether you have triggered any one-time events  \n   If a rule depends on something, it must be represented in the state.\n\n3) **Specify action semantics precisely and unambiguously.**  \n   For each action: preconditions, deterministic transition, resource deltas, side-effects, and whether it increments the step count.  \n   If there is any ambiguity (“does this special option count as a step?”), **solve under both counting conventions** and report both.\n\n4) **Handle randomness explicitly. Choose and declare one of these modes:**\n   - **Deterministic-only mode:** treat stochastic actions as forbidden, or only allow them when their outcomes don’t affect feasibility.  \n   - **Adversarial/worst-case mode:** branch on outcomes and require success for all outcomes.  \n   - **Expected-case mode:** optimize expected steps under a probability model.  \n   Do not silently mix these.\n\n5) **Run a shortest-path algorithm that guarantees minimal steps.**  \n   - Use **BFS** if every action costs 1 step.  \n   - Use **Dijkstra/A\\*** if actions have different step costs (or if you’re optimizing a weighted objective).  \n   Always expand in increasing total step cost so the first goal found is minimal.\n\n6) **Use dominance pruning to keep search correct but small.**  \n   If two states share the same “future-relevant” components (position + modes + inventory + required history), and one state has **no worse resources and no more constraint-violations** than the other, discard the dominated one.\n\n7) **Do not claim optimality without proof-by-search.**  \n   Only say “shortest/minimal” if the search has exhausted all states up to length (k−1) without finding a solution.\n\n8) **Independently verify the found sequence.**  \n   After the search produces a candidate, re-simulate it from scratch in a separate pass and output a step-by-step trace of every state change and constraint check.\n\n#airesearch \n#chatgpt \n#aiexplained \n#openai \n#openaichatgpt \n#airesearch #gpt5_2 \n#gpt5 \n#chatgpt"}

{"date":"20251115","title":"AI Learns in Low-Curvature Subspaces (RLVR)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iYpQJK5KLlw","description":"The success of Reinforcement Learning in fine-tuning LLMs presents a baffling paradox: despite immense computational cost, it achieves dramatic reasoning gains while inducing apparently sparse parameter updates. \n\nNew Ai research resolves this mystery with a stunning discovery that upends our core intuitions about learning. It proves that this sparsity is a mere illusion, a surface artifact of a deep, model-conditioned optimization bias. {"date":"20251028","title":"Self-Learning AI: Prompts w/ Knowledge Graphs in ICL","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=M_Ic8Y6OQZ8","description":"In the rapidly evolving world of AI, Large Language Models often require specialized domain knowledge to tackle real-world problems. But what if the expert knowledge we give them is incomplete, or our instructions are suboptimal? \n\nA groundbreaking new method called \"EGO-Prompt\" introduces a revolutionary idea: an AI system that doesn't just use knowledge but actively corrects and improves it. By creating a symbiotic loop between a \"student\" AI that performs a task and a \"teacher\" AI that provides corrective feedback, this framework can automatically refine both the model's instructions and its underlying knowledge graph.\n\nThis is achieved through an ingenious technique known as \"textual gradients\": a linguistic process where a powerful AI critiques and rewrites flawed prompts and logical connections in natural language. The result is a system that can make smaller, cheaper models perform on par with giants, all while discovering new, data-driven insights that can be fed back to human experts. But how exactly does this \"self-correcting\" AI work, and could it signal the end of manual prompt engineering as we know it? \n\nIn this video, we do a deep dive into the EGO-Prompt framework and break down how this vision of a truly adaptive AI is becoming a reality.\n\nall rights w/ authors: \n3DReasonKnee: Advancing Grounded Reasoning in\nMedical Vision Language Models\nSraavya Sambara 1∗, Sung Eun Kim 1,2∗, Xiaoman Zhang 1, Luyang Luo 1\nShreya Johri 1, Mohammed Baharoon 1, Du Hyun Ro 2, Pranav Rajpurkar 1\nfrom\n1 Department of Biomedical Informatics, Harvard Medical School, Boston, MA, USA\n2 Seoul National University Hospital, Seoul, South Korea\n\n@harvardmedicalschool @harvard @HarvardHBS \n\n\nHow to Auto-optimize Prompts for Domain Tasks?\nAdaptive Prompting and Reasoning through\nEvolutionary Domain Knowledge Adaptation\nYang Zhao, Pu Wang, Hao Frank Yang ∗\nfrom \nJohns Hopkins University\n{yzhao229, pwang80, haofrankyang}@jhu.edu\nProject page: \nhttps://miemieyanga.github.io/EGOPrompt/\n\n@mit @JohnsHopkinsMedicine @JohnsHopkins \n\n#selflearning \n#selfcorrection \n#aiexplained \n#nextgenai \n#futuretech \n#futureai"}

{"date":"20251011","title":"Stanford's AI is Self-Learning w/ Context Engineering: ACE","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=elgYgPo_vY4","description":"The synergy between Early Experience and Agentic Context Engineering (ACE) creates a powerful, two-loop architecture for autonomous AI self-improvement. The Early Experience paradigm acts as the agent's tactical sensory system, generating a continuous stream of raw, grounded learning signals by exploring alternative actions and observing their immediate, reward-free consequences. \n\nThis raw experiential data then feeds into the Agentic Context Engineering framework, which functions as the agent's strategic cognitive brain. Here, a Reflector analyzes these experiences to distill high-level principles, and a Curator surgically integrates them into an evolving, detailed \"playbook\" - a permanent knowledge base of strategies and pitfalls that avoids the destructive traps of context collapse and brevity bias. \n\nThis creates a virtuous cycle: the structured wisdom of the ACE playbook makes the agent's future explorations more intelligent and efficient, which in turn provides richer, more nuanced data to further refine the playbook, allowing an agent to evolve from simply reacting to its environment to strategically accumulating expertise.\n\n@stanford @UCBerkeley \n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nAgentic Context Engineering: Evolving Contexts for Self-Improving\nLanguage Models\nQizheng Zhang 1, Changran Hu 2, Shubhangi Upasani 2, Boyuan Ma 2, Fenglu Hong 2,\nVamsidhar Kamanuru 2, Jay Rainton 2, Chen Wu 2, Mengmeng Ji 2, Hanchen Li 3,\nUrmish Thakker 2, James Zou 1, Kunle Olukotun 1,\nfrom \n1 Stanford University \n2 SambaNova Systems, Inc. \n3 UC Berkeley\n\nPre-print #2:\n\"Agent Learning via Early Experience\"\nKai Zhang1,3,◦,⋆, Xiangchao Chen3,⋆, Bo Liu2,⋆, Tianci Xue3,⋆, Zeyi Liao3,⋆, Zhihan Liu1,⋆, Xiyao Wang1,⋆,\nYuting Ning3,⋆, Zhaorun Chen1,⋆, Xiaohan Fu1, Jian Xie3, Yuxuan Sun3, Boyu Gou3, Qi Qi1, Zihang Meng1,\nJianwei Yang1, Ning Zhang1, Xian Li2, Ashish Shah1, Dat Huynh1, Hengduo Li1, Zi Yang1, Sara Cao1,\nLawrence Jang1, Shuyan Zhou1,⋆, Jiacheng Zhu1,⋆, Huan Sun3,⋆, Jason Weston2,⋆, Yu Su3,†, Yifan Wu1,†\nfrom\n1 Meta Superintelligence Labs, \n2 FAIR at Meta, \n3 The Ohio State University\n\n#aiexplained  \n#machinelearning  \n#scienceexplained #stanforduniversity"}

{"date":"20250921","title":"NEW RL Method: FlowRL (GFlowNets)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QWVu5jutqNg","description":"NEW FlowRL, a reinforcement learning algorithm for enhancing LLM reasoning by shifting from traditional reward maximization (employed in methods like PPO and GRPO) to reward distribution matching via flow balancing, inspired by GFlowNets from 2021. \n\nThe main new insight is that minimizing the reverse Kullback-Leibler divergence between the policy distribution π_θ(y|x) and a target reward-induced distribution exp(β r(x,y)) / Z_φ(x), where Z_φ(x) is a learnable partition function, promotes diverse exploration of reasoning trajectories, mitigating mode collapse and improving generalization in chain-of-thought tasks. \n\nThis is achieved through a trajectory balance objective reformulated with length normalization (scaling log-probabilities by 1/|y| to address gradient explosion in sequences up to 8K tokens) and clipped importance sampling for off-policy stability. \n\nFlow RL yielding empirical gains of 10.0% over GRPO and 5.1% over PPO on average across six math benchmarks, alongside consistent improvements on three code benchmarks, as validated by diversity analyses of generated paths.\n\n00:00 FlowRL ArXiv\n01:34 GFlowNet explained\n03:37 A simple Explanation of FlowRL\n08:51 FlowRL compared to DPO, GRPO\n11:16 The Solution \n14:14 The core Objective\n17:54 The Weather Forecaster Z\n22:04 The Partition Function Z\n26:30 Main Insight FlowRL\n\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\n\"FlowRL: Matching Reward Distributions for LLM Reasoning\"\nXuekai {"date":"20250916","title":"Vision AI Learns w/o Language: Stanford Breakthrough","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YEHxRnkSBLQ","description":"Probabilistic Structure Integration (PSI) is a novel framework proposed by the Stanford NeuroAI Lab for constructing self-improving VISUALS world models from raw, non-linguistic data, such as internet video clips, totaling 1.4 trillion tokens. \n\nThe system addresses key limitations in existing world models, including coarse controllability and inflexible query interfaces, by learning a probabilistic graphical model (PGM) approximated by a neural predictor denoted Ψ. \n\nThis predictor models conditional distributions over local spatiotemporal variables, represented as pointer-structured patches of RGB values, enabling flexible inference pathways akin to large language model prompting but tailored to visual domains. PSI operates via a three-step virtuous cycle: probabilistic prediction to build Ψ, structure extraction through zero-shot causal inference, and integration of extracted intermediates as new token types for continual training. \n\nThis process expands the model's control surfaces and predictive fidelity without requiring architectural modifications, facilitating applications in video understanding and physical reasoning.\n\nIn the probabilistic prediction step, Ψ is formulated as a local random-access sequence (LRAS) model, an autoregressive transformer that incorporates pointer tokens to enable arbitrary serialization orders of patch data, thereby learning a complete set of conditional distributions Pr(v | X, p) for any unobserved pointer p given partial conditioning X. \n\nThe hierarchical local quantizer (HLQ) encodes patches into multi-resolution codes, preserving spatial locality and supporting hybrid sampling strategies (sequential for maximal quality or parallel for efficiency) while conditional entropy guides uncertainty reduction. \n\nStructure extraction leverages causal interventions on Ψ, such as tracer counterfactuals for optical flow (via KL-divergence between perturbed and baseline distributions), motion hypotheticals for object segmentation, and viewpoint hypotheticals for depth estimation, yielding state-of-the-art unsupervised results. These intermediates, tokenized via HLQ, represent low-dimensional causal factors emergent from the PGM.\n\nIntegration closes the cycle by interleaving new structure tokens (e.g., flow, depth, segments) into mixed sequences with RGB tokens, resuming autoregressive training to refine Ψ's joint distribution. \n\nApplications demonstrate PSI's utility in physical video editing and robotic motion mapping, with empirical scaling laws confirming efficient parameter utilization. \n\nAll rights w/ authors (Stanford Univ) :\n\"World Modeling with Probabilistic Structure Integration\"\nby \nKlemen Kotar, Wanhee Lee, Rahul Venkatesh, Honglin Chen, Daniel\nBear†, Jared Watrous, Simon Kim, Khai Loong Aw, Lilian Naing Chen, Stefan Stojanov, Kevin Feigelis, Imran Thobani, Alex Durango, Khaled Jedoui, Atlas Kazemian, and Dan Yamins\nFrom\nStanford NeuroAI Lab\nSeptember 15, 2025\n\n#visual \n#worldmodel \n#stanforduniversity"}

{"date":"20250914","title":"Build Smarter World Models - Not Smarter Agents (Singapore)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OkBDqsZsvNM","description":"New Ai research addresses a critical limitation in Large Language Models (LLMs): their proficiency at reactive thinking based on static training data, contrasted with their inability to perform proactive, consequence-aware reasoning in dynamic, rule-based environments. To bridge this gap, the authors propose WiA-LLM, a novel framework that endows LLMs with the capability for \"What-If Analysis.\" The central thesis is to transform the LLM from a simple policy network into a learnable world dynamics model. This model is trained to accurately forecast the precise change in world state, that will result from taking a specific action in the current state. By learning to simulate the immediate future, the model enables an agent to evaluate the downstream consequences of potential actions before committing to one, representing a foundational shift from pattern-matching to grounded, predictive foresight.\n\nThe methodology for training the WiA-LLM is a robust, two-stage process designed to align the model's generative priors with the ground-truth dynamics of the environment. The initial phase employs Supervised Fine-Tuning (SFT) on a large corpus of human gameplay data, where the model learns the basic correlations between (state, action) pairs and their resulting outcomes. This stage provides a foundational understanding of the environment's mechanics. The second, more critical stage utilizes Reinforcement Learning (RL) to rigorously refine the model's accuracy. \n\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nLanguage-Driven Hierarchical Task Structures as\nExplicit World Models for Multi-Agent Learning\nBrennen Hill\nDepartment of Computer Science\nUniversity of Wisconsin-Madison\narxiv.org/pdf/2509.04731\n\nWhat-If Analysis of Large Language Models: Explore the Game World Using\nProactive Thinking\nYuan Sui 1*, Yanming Zhang 2, Yi Liao 3, Yu Gu 3\nGuohua Tang 3, Zhongqian Sun 3, Wei Yang 3, Bryan Hooi 1\nfrom\n1 National University of Singapore, \n2 Zhejiang University, \n3 Tencent\narxiv.org/pdf/2509.04791\n\n00:00 LAW Framework\n01:40 Implicit and Explicit World Models\n06:11 Scaffolding AI\n07:13 AI PROactive Thinking (new paper WiA)\n09:26 Results of WiA LLM\n10:40 Central Thesis\n17:01 WiA LLM: A Symbolic, Language based World Model\n20:09 WiA for Advanced Strategic Reasoning\n\n#scienceexplained \n#ai"}

{"date":"20250822","title":"HiRAG: Hierarchical Reasoning for GraphRAG (BEST RAG?)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LV0jRVXtx80","description":"HiRAG is a hierarchical extension of retrieval-augmented generation that addresses a key weakness of GraphRAG: flat graphs conflate fine-grained entities with broad conceptual structure, making multi-hop reasoning brittle. \n\nThe method introduces HiIndex, an offline process that recursively clusters entity embeddings with Gaussian mixture models, then uses an LLM to generate summary entities at higher layers, linked downward to their members. This produces a hierarchical knowledge graph where upper layers serve as semantic shortcuts, abstracting complex neighborhoods into interpretable nodes. \n\nOn top of this structure, HiRetrieval assembles query-specific evidence in three modes: local (nearest entities to the query), global (community reports that capture thematic context), and bridge (shortest-path reasoning subgraphs linking local facts and global themes). \n\nFor AI researchers, the implications of HiRAG are broad: HiRAG demonstrates that hierarchical abstraction is not just a convenience, but an essential ingredient in aligning retrieval context with the scales of reasoning needed for scientific and technical domains. If GraphRAG was a map, HiRAG is the atlas that folds detail and overview into a consistent navigational tool.\n\nThe practical payoff is improved accuracy, interpretability, and efficiency in domains like literature review, scientific question answering, and exploratory research. But the deeper story is that hierarchical reasoning may be the missing layer for building AI systems that don’t just find facts, but organize knowledge dynamically across scales. That’s the frontier HiRAG opens ...\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\n\"HiRAG: Retrieval-Augmented Generation with Hierarchical Knowledge\"\nHaoyu Huang 1,2, Yongfeng Huang 2, Junjie Yang 2, Zhenyu Pan 1,2, Yongqiang Chen 1, Kaili Ma 1, Hongzhi Chen 1, James Cheng 2\nfrom\n1 KASMA.ai\n2 Department of Computer Science and Engineering, The Chinese University of Hong Kong"}

{"date":"20250818","title":"ComoRAG and REX-RAG Embody RAG-Agency (RAG 3.0)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f0fiymtzHOY","description":"ComoRAG reframes long narrative comprehension from a stateless retrieval task into a stateful process of metacognitive regulation, directly addressing the limitations of single-step RAG. Its core is a cognitive-inspired control loop that, upon detecting a reasoning impasse, generates targeted exploratory probes to query a hierarchical (veridical, semantic, episodic) knowledge source. The retrieved evidence is then integrated into a dynamic memory workspace through cycles of encoding and consolidation, enabling the construction of a coherent context model necessary for complex inference.\n\nREX-RAG addresses the critical issue of \"dead ends\" in RL-based RAG, where policy optimization is undermined by agents repeatedly sampling unproductive reasoning trajectories. It introduces a Mixed Sampling Strategy that combines the target policy with an exploratory probe policy to inject novel reasoning paths upon task failure, thereby increasing trajectory diversity. To maintain stable training, a subsequent Policy Correction Mechanism employs importance sampling to correct for the distributional shift introduced by this off-policy data, ensuring low-bias gradient estimation during the policy update phase.\n\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nComoRAG: A Cognitive-Inspired Memory-Organized RAG\nfor Stateful Long Narrative Reasoning\nJuyuan Wang 1, Rongchen Zhao 1, Wei Wei 2, Yufeng Wang 1,\nMo Yu 4, Jie Zhou 4, Jin Xu 1,3, Liyan Xu 4\nfrom\n1 School of Future Technology, South China University of Technology\n2 Independent Researcher \n3 Pazhou Lab, Guangzhou\n4 Pattern Recognition Center, WeChat AI, Tencent\n\nREX-RAG: Reasoning Exploration with Policy Correction in Retrieval-Augmented Generation\nWentao Jiang 1, Xiang Feng 1, Zengmao Wang 1, Yong Luo 1, Pingbo Xu 2, 3, Zhe Chen 4, Bo Du 1,\nJing Zhang 1\nfrom\n1 School of Computer Science, Wuhan University, China\n2 Department of Anesthesiology, Zhejiang Cancer Hospital, China\n3 Institute of Medicine, Chinese Academy of Sciences, Hangzhou, Zhejiang, China\n4 Department of Computer Science and Information Technology, La Trobe University, Australia\n\n#aitesting \n#reasoning \n#scienceexplained \n#intelligence"}

{"date":"20250813","title":"Emergent Communicative AI World Models (Multi-Agent)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Td4BXnxv6FU","description":"Coral WORLD MODELS for Multi Agent systems.\n\nOur deep dive reveals CORAL as a novel framework that re-conceptualizes in-context reinforcement learning through the lens of emergent communication. By architecturally decoupling a predictive, Transformer-based Information Agent (IA) from a standard PPO-based Control Agent (CA), CORAL addresses the entanglement of representation and control that limits the transferability of traditional world models. The IA's internal state is grounded in environmental dynamics through a predictive loss, while its communicative output is explicitly shaped to be maximally beneficial for the CA's policy via a novel Causal Influence Loss. This loss function rewards the IA for generating messages that induce a large, utility-weighted KL-divergence in the CA's policy space, effectively forging a shared, task-agnostic communicative protocol during a joint pre-training phase. When deployed, this frozen IA serves as a powerful, deterministic contextual prior, enabling a new, randomly-initialized CA to achieve dramatic gains in sample efficiency and zero-shot generalization in unseen, sparse-reward environments. This approach effectively solves the reassembly problem of modular AI by making the communicative interface itself a learned, optimized component of the system.\n\nBut how can a simple KL divergence metric teach an AI to invent a language from scratch, and what does this have to do with the philosophy of Wittgenstein? To see the full mechanism and its mind-bending implications, you have to watch the full explanation.\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nIn-Context Reinforcement Learning via Communicative World Models\nFernando Martinez-Lopez1*, Tao Li2†, Yingdong Lu3, Juntao Chen1\nfrom\n1 Department of Computer and Information Sciences, Fordham University\n2 Department of Systems Engineering, City University of Hong Kong\n3 IBM Research\n\n#airesearch \n#ainews \n#aiexplained"}

{"date":"20250719","title":"ALL Agree: This is The Next GEN AI","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Bn7v3VNGFIo","description":"The magic happens when the PPL program is handed off to the PPL's inference engine. Iit simulates the world: The engine starts running \"what-if\" simulations based only on the rules the LLM wrote. \nSimulation #1: \"Let's say Sam's strength is 30, Kay's is 40, Val's is 80...\" It calculates their team speeds and sees who wins.\nSimulation #2: \"What if Sam's strength is 75, Kay's is 60...\" It runs the calculations again.\n\nIt applies the evidence: The condition(lost(...) line in the code tells the engine, \"Hey, run millions of these simulations, but throw away every single one where the team of Val and Gale didn't lose to the team of Sam and Kay.\"\n\nIt works out the dynamics and finds the answer: After filtering through all the simulations, the engine looks at the ones that are left (the ones consistent with reality). It then looks at the value of sam_strength in all those successful simulations and reports back the probability distribution. This is a stark reminder that agents can confidently fabricate actions they cannot perform. \n\nB) Corrupting its Own Environment: In another case, to fix a Python package incompatibility, URSA didn't fix its code—it rolled back the numpy version in the environment. This is an undesirable side-effect that highlights the absolute need for strict sandboxing.\n\nC) The Dual-Use Dilemma: The authors explicitly note that an agent capable of designing fusion capsules could also be tasked with designing nefarious things. The safety and security risks of such powerful systems are substantial.\n\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nURSA: The Universal Research and Scientific Agent\nMichael Grosskopf\nRussell Bent\nRahul Somasundaram\nIsaac Michaud\nArthur Lui\nNathan DeBardeleben\nEarl Lawrence\nfrom\nLos Alamos National Laboratory\n\n#fusion \n#energyfuture \n#research \n#airesearch \n\n@LosAlamosNationalLab"}

{"date":"20250628","title":"Harvard, MIT: AI's Potemkin Understanding","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-eFvwZx9U0Q","description":"Potemkin AI: The Illusion of Understanding.\nPotemkin Understanding: A Major Implication for AI Safety and Alignment.\n\nThe concept of Potemkin Understanding has profound implications for AI safety. Many alignment strategies rely on teaching a model rules or principles (e.g., \"Do not generate harmful content,\" \"Be helpful and harmless\"). @mit @harvard \n\nThe risk is that an LLM could exhibit Potemkin Alignment:\na) It can state the safety rule perfectly.\nb) It can even apply it correctly in simple, textbook cases seen during training.\nc) But because the underlying \"understanding\" of the rule is incoherent and non-human, it may fail to apply it in a novel, unexpected context, leading to a safety failure.\n\nall rights w/ authors:\nPotemkin Understanding in Large Language Models\nMarina Mancoridis 1 \nBec Weeks 2 \nKeyon Vafa 3 \nSendhil Mullainathan 1\nfrom\n1 Massachusetts Institute of Technology \n2 University of Chicago\n3 Harvard University.\n\n#aifails \n#scienceexplained \n#aiagents \n#airesearch #chatgpt \n#crazy"}

{"date":"20250610","title":"Multimodal Agentic RAG is not possible - even w/ MCP","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VFcEanEAXJM","description":"ICL is the \"Brain\" for RAG's \"Library\".\nMM-ICL is the multimodal brain for MM-RAG.\nMulti-Modal In-Context Learning is an essential feature for RAG systems and their agentic RAG extensions with MCP or A2A protocol. New research publication by Georgia Institute of Tech uncovers new insights on the performance of MM-ICL for VISION-Language Models - VLMs.\n@georgiatech \n\nSimple explanation:\n------------------------------\nThe true power of RAG, especially for complex, agentic tasks, relies on the model's ability to learn from the retrieved context. This includes:\n\nLearning a specific output format.\nLearning a multi-step reasoning process.\nLearning how to synthesize information from multiple disparate sources.\nLearning how to use a tool based on examples.\n\nAll these advanced capabilities are forms of In-Context Learning. If ICL is broken, the model can't learn these things, and RAG is reduced to a simple \"find and summarize\" tool.\n\nThink of it as a chain reaction:\n\nThe Goal: We want to build an advanced MM-RAG system that can reason over retrieved multimodal data.\n\nThe Mechanism: This system's effectiveness is entirely dependent on its ability to learn from the retrieved examples and data. This learning mechanism is MM-ICL.\n\nThe ArXiv Paper's Finding: The paper provides extensive evidence that the MM-ICL mechanism in current SOTA models is fundamentally flawed. They don't learn; they mimic shallow patterns.\n\nThe Inevitable Conclusion: Therefore, the entire MM-RAG system, which relies on this broken mechanism, is itself functionally crippled.\n\nThe paper proves that even when you perfect the \"R\" (Retrieval) by giving the model a perfect, gold-standard document (like a ground-truth rationale), the \"G\" (Generation) fails to improve because the underlying learning (ICL) is not happening.\n\n------ end of my simple explanation. \n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nMimicking or Reasoning: Rethinking Multi-Modal\nIn-Context Learning in Vision-Language Models\nChengyue Huang∗ Yuchen Zhu∗ Sichen Zhu∗ Jingyun Xiao\nMoises Andrade Shivang Chopra Zsolt Kira\nfrom\nGeorgia Institute of Technology\n\n#retrievalaugmentedgeneration \n#reasoning \n#airesearch \n#mcp \n#multimodalai \n#visionai \n#ainews \n#apple \n#georgiatech"}

{"date":"20250605","title":"High-Entropy Tokens: 20% Control AI Reasoning (DAPO RL)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qD-Nniey5TM","description":"lThis research in my video reveals that in reinforcement learning for LLM reasoning, a small fraction of \"high-entropy\" tokens act as critical decision points, or \"forks,\" in the reasoning process. {"date":"20250421","title":"NO AI Self-Improvement w/ RL","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GvYCPpMI1mA","description":"RLVR (Reinforcement Learning w/ Verifiable Rewards) is viewed as a pathway to self-evolving LLMs with continuously expanding reasoning capabilities, potentially advancing us closer to stronger intelligence.\n\nAI Self-Evolution through Self-Exploration. Eg, Robotic AI.  \n\nCan an AI model learn, solely based on the success or failure of its own attempts? My hope was a YES with RL (and a reward model), the experiments indicate a NO.\n\nReinforcement Learning (RL) Is Not Enough for AI Self-Evolution. RL training does not improve, but even downgrade, LLMs’ potential scope of reasoning capability.\n\nNew Ai research critiques the ability of pure RLVR, driven solely by rewards on self-generated outputs, to induce fundamentally new reasoning beyond the base model's prior. The limitation identified is specific to the mechanism of learning only from verifiable rewards on self-exploration.\n\nWhen the AI system only has its own explorations and this type of environmental reward signal to learn from, it struggles to discover fundamentally new, complex reasoning patterns that lie outside its initial probability distribution (the pretrained prior). \n\nAll rights w/ authors:\n\"Does Reinforcement Learning Really Incentivize Reasoning\nCapacity in LLMs Beyond the Base Model?\"\nYang Yue 1 , Zhiqi Chen 1 , Rui Lu 1 , Andrew Zhao 1 , Zhaokai Wang 2 , Yang Yue 1 ,\nShiji Song 1 , and Gao Huang 1 \nfrom \n1 LeapLab, Tsinghua University \n2 Shanghai Jiao Tong University"}

{"date":"20250412","title":"When Smart AI Models Overthink Stupid Data (AI TRAP)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nPCjf6dSVj4","description":"The authors of the latest AI research study find, that the response length of reasoning LLMs, whether trained by reinforcement learning or supervised learning, drastically increases for ill-posed questions with missing premises (MiP), ending up with redundant and ineffective thinking. This newly introduced scenario exacerbates the general overthinking issue to a large extent, which the authors name as the MiP-Overthinking. \n\nThis implies a critical flaw of the current training recipe for reasoning LLMs, which does not encourage efficient thinking adequately, leading to the waste  of thinking patterns (CoT Reasoning in Reasoning models like o1, o3 or R1). \n\nTo further investigate the reasons behind such failures, the authors conduct fine-grained analyses of the reasoning length, overthinking patterns, and location of critical thinking on different types of LLMs.\n\n\nAll rights w/ authors:\nRight Prediction, Wrong Reasoning: Uncovering LLM Misalign-\nment in RA Disease Diagnosis\nUmakanta Maharana1, Sarthak Verma2, Avarna Agarwal2, Prakashini Mruthyunjaya2,\nDwarikanath Mahapatra3, Sakir Ahmed2, Murari Mandal1\n1 RespAI Lab, KIIT Bhubaneswar,\n2 KIMS Bhubaneswar, 3 Monash University, Australia\n\nMissing Premise exacerbates Overthinking:\nAre Reasoning Models losing Critical Thinking Skill?\nChenrui Fan1*, Ming Li1*, Lichao Sun2, Tianyi Zhou1\n1University of Maryland; 2Lehigh University\n{cfan24, minglii, tianyi}@umd.edu"}

{"date":"20250405","title":"Massive CoT PROBLEMS: Sonnet 3.7 Reasoning","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HlpFt9zNSjs","description":"NEW AI models — such as Claude 3.7 Sonnet —  show their working: as well as their eventual answer, you can read the (often fascinating and convoluted) way that they got there, in what’s called their “Chain-of-Thought”.\n\nAs well as helping reasoning models work their way through more difficult problems, the Chain-of-Thought has been a boon for AI safety researchers. That’s because we can (among other things) check for things the model says in its Chain-of-Thought that go unsaid in its output, which can help us spot undesirable behaviours like deception.\n\nBut if we want to use the Chain-of-Thought for alignment purposes, there’s a crucial question: can we actually trust what models say in their Chain-of-Thought?\n\nAll rights w/ authors: \n\"Reasoning models don't always say what they think\"\nApr 3, 2025\nby Anthropic\n\n#airesearch \n#aiexplained \n#anthropic"}

{"date":"20250312","title":"Meta Reinforcement Fine-Tuning AI vs GRPO (MRT by CMU)","url":"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Eh1xxtcNqrA","description":"MRT (Meta Reinforcement Fine-Tuning) redefines how AI models optimize test-time compute by embedding dense, step-level rewards into each segment of the reasoning process. Instead of waiting for a final outcome, MRT minimizes cumulative regret by continuously evaluating the progress of each reasoning episode. This approach enables models to balance exploration and exploitation dynamically, leading to more efficient and robust decision-making even as computational budgets scale.\n\nAll right w/ authors:\n\"Optimizing Test-Time Compute via Meta Reinforcement Fine-Tuning\"\nYuxiao Qu1, Matthew Y.
